## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes CNI Network Plugin Interface Architecture

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the CNI (Container Network Interface) integration: the CNI plugin invocation, the network namespace setup, the IP address management (IPAM) call, and the network plugin manager that coordinates CNI calls during pod creation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

I am thinking...: I'm not finding any in-tree CNI plugin code in Kubernetes v1.32. This is expected because:

1. The kubenet plugin (which was the in-tree CNI plugin) was removed in Kubernetes v1.24 (it was deprecated in v1.23)
2. The dockershim was removed in v1.24
3. In v1.32, CNI is handled entirely by the container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) via the CRI interface

So the CNI integration in Kubernetes v1.32 is:
1. The kubelet calls `RunPodSandbox` via CRI (in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go`)
2. The CRI client sends the request to the container runtime (in `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`)
3. The container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) then calls the CNI plugins

The actual CNI plugin invocation, network namespace setup, and IPAM calls are NOT in the Kubernetes codebase in v1.32 - they are in the container runtime (containerd or CRI-O).

However, there might be some CNI-related code in the vendor directory. Let me check if there's any CNI library code vendored.

922026-03-08T19:37:13.630725agentmessage-
Here is the complete, definitive list of Go source files in **kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.0** that implement CNI network plugin integration, along with the precise role each plays.

---

## Architectural Context

**Kubernetes v1.32.0 has no in-tree CNI implementation.** The `pkg/kubelet/network/cni/` and `pkg/kubelet/dockershim/` directories were removed. All CNI plugin invocation, network namespace setup, and IPAM calls are fully delegated to the container runtime (containerd, CRI-O) via the **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**. The kubelet communicates with the runtime over gRPC; the runtime then calls CNI binaries on the kubelet's behalf.

The call chain is:
```
kubelet (SyncPod)
  → kuberuntime_manager.go (createPodSandbox)
    → kuberuntime_sandbox.go (m.runtimeService.RunPodSandbox)
      → instrumented_services.go (metrics wrapper)
        → remote_runtime.go (gRPC → container runtime)
          → [containerd/CRI-O invokes CNI plugin, sets up netns, runs IPAM]
            → returns PodSandboxNetworkStatus with assigned IPs
```

---

## The Files

### 1. CRI API Contract — Network Primitives

**`staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1/api.proto`**
The canonical source of truth for all network-related CRI messages:
- `PodSandboxNetworkStatus` (lines 547–552): IP address(es) returned by the runtime after CNI runs
- `NamespaceOption` / `NamespaceMode`: `POD` vs `NODE` (host network) — controls whether the runtime creates a new netns or shares the host's
- `NetworkConfig` / `RuntimeConfig` (lines 1567–1575): carries `pod_cidr` pushed from kubelet to runtime via `UpdateRuntimeConfig`
- `RuntimeCondition` (lines 1596+): defines `RuntimeReady` and `NetworkReady` conditions the kubelet polls to gate pod scheduling

**`staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/apis/runtime/v1

The key findings are fully documented in my previous response:

**The critical architectural fact**: Kubernetes v1.32.0 contains **zero in-tree CNI code**. There is no `pkg/kubelet/network/cni/`, no vendored `github.com/containernetworking/cni`, and no kubenet plugin. CNI plugin invocation, network namespace setup, and IPAM are entirely owned by the container runtime (containerd/CRI-O), which the kubelet reaches exclusively via CRI gRPC.

**The 14 relevant Go source files** span four layers:
1. **CRI API contract** (`api.proto`, `api.pb.go`, `services.go`) — defines the network messages
2. **CRI gRPC client** (`remote_runtime.go`) — the actual `RunPodSandbox` call that triggers CNI
3. **Kubelet runtime manager** (`kuberuntime_sandbox.go`, `kuberuntime_manager.go`, `instrumented_services.go`, `util/util.go`) — orchestrates sandbox creation and reads back CNI-assigned IPs
4. **Kubelet network state** (`kubelet_network.go`, `kubelet_network_linux.go`, `runtime.go`, `kubelet.go`, `container/runtime.go`, `metrics/metrics.go`) — tracks network readiness, propagates pod CIDR, gates pod admission

{
  "thought": "I'm not finding any in-tree CNI plugin code in Kubernetes v1.32. This is expected because:\n\n1. The kubenet plugin (which was the in-tree CNI plugin) was removed in Kubernetes v1.24 (it was deprecated in v1.23)\n2. The dockershim was removed in v1.24\n3. In v1.32, CNI is handled entirely by the container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) via the CRI interface\n\nSo the CNI integration in Kubernetes v1.32 is:\n1. The kubelet calls `RunPodSandbox` via CRI (in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_sandbox.go`)\n2. The CRI client sends the request to the container runtime (in `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-client/pkg/remote_runtime.go`)\n3. The container runtime (containerd/CRI-O) then calls the CNI plugins\n\nThe actual CNI plugin invocation, network namespace setup, and IPAM calls are NOT in the Kubernetes codebase in v1.32 - they are in the container runtime (containerd or CRI-O).\n\nHowever, there might be some CNI-related code in the vendor directory. Let me check if there's any CNI library code vendored.\n\nActually, let me look at the vendor directory for any CNI-related packages."
